# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Kubernetes API Server Architecture and Extension Guide

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a subsystem architecture and extension guide for the apiserver library with request-path flow and extension tradeoffs.

## Scope

Focus on the Kubernetes apiserver library subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.


## Artifact-Only Evaluation

You are in **artifact-only mode**. Your workspace is empty — all code discovery
must go through Sourcegraph MCP tools. Express all code changes as **unified
diffs** in your output artifact (e.g., `fix_patch` fields in review.json, or a
standalone `solution.patch` file). Do NOT attempt to edit source files directly
— there are no source files in your workspace.

{"content":"1: # apiserver Architecture\n2: \n3: ## 1. Server Composition\n4: \n5: The `kube-apiserver` binary is not one server, but a **server chain** of three distinct\n6: `GenericAPIServer` instances: the core Kubernetes API, API extensions (CRDs), and the aggregation\n7: layer.\n8: \n9: This composition is managed by a layered configuration system, starting with command-line\n10: flags parsed by `options` structs (e.g., `RecommendedOptions` in `pkg/server/options`), which\n11: populate a `Config` object that is then used to instantiate the `GenericAPIServer`\n12: instances. The construction of this delegation chain can be found in the `CreateServerChain`\n13: function in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go`.\n14: \n15: ```mermaid\n16: graph TD\n17:     subgraph Incoming Request\n18:         direction LR\n19:         A[User/Client] --> B{/apis/apps/v1/deployments};\n20:     end\n21: \n22:     subgraph kube-apiserver process\n23:         direction LR\n24:         B --> C[Aggregator Server];\n25:         C -- Not an APIService --> D[Kube API Server];\n26:         D -- Handles Request --> E[REST Storage];\n27:         C -- Is an APIService --> F[Proxy to Extension API Server];\n28:         D -- Not a Core API --> G[API Extensions Server];\n29:         G -- Handles CRD --> E;\n30:     end\n31: ```\n32: \n33: 1.  **Aggregator Server (`kube-aggregator`):**\n34:     *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiregistration.k8s.io` API and acts as a reverse proxy for\n35:         extension API servers. This functionality was designed to allow third-party APIs to be\n36:         \"aggregated\" into the main Kubernetes API server seamlessly.\n37:     *   **Mechanism:** It watches `APIService` objects. When a request arrives (e.g., for\n38:         `/apis/mycompany.com/v1/myresources`), it

## Key Sections:

1. **Subsystem Purpose & Boundaries** - The apiserver library's role, dependencies, and scope
2. **Key Components** - 8 major subsystems with responsibilities:
   - GenericAPIServer orchestration
   - Handler chain pipeline (15 filter stages)
   - Endpoint installation and REST handlers
   - Admission control framework
   - Authentication/Authorization plugins
   - Storage abstraction layer
   - API group registration
   - Watch cache performance optimization

3. **End-to-End Request Flow** - Concrete traced examples with file references:
   - GET request flow through handler chain
   - Watch (streaming) request handling
   - POST create with admission/validation
   - Storage operations through cacher and etcd3

4. **Failure Modes & Design Tradeoffs** - 8 operational considerations:
   - Concurrency fairness via flow control
   - Watch cache consistency guarantees
   - Request timeout and resource limits
   - Optimistic locking and conflict resolution
   - Admission webhook latency risks
   - etcd overload scenarios
   - Storage transformation overhead
   - Discovery spec performance

5. **Extension Points** - 9 customization hooks with code examples:
   - Custom authentication
   - Custom authorization
   - Admission webhooks and plugins
   - RESTStorage backends
   - Handler chain wrapping
   - Request info parsing
   - Lifecycle hooks (post-start, pre-shutdown)
   - Storage backends

6. **Operational Implications** - Performance characteristics:
   - Memory usage (watch cache as primary consumer)
   - Latency profile and bottlenecks
   - Throughput limits (5-10K reads/sec typical)
   - Gracef

Server Composition\\n4: \\n5: The `kube-apiserver` binary is not one server, but a **server chain** of three distinct\\n6: `GenericAPIServer` instances: the core Kubernetes API, API extensions (CRDs), and the aggregation\\n7: layer.\\n8: \\n9: This composition is managed by a layered configuration system, starting with command-line\\n10: flags parsed by `options` structs (e.g., `RecommendedOptions` in `pkg/server/options`), which\\n11: populate a `Config` object that is then used to instantiate the `GenericAPIServer`\\n12: instances. The construction of this delegation chain can be found in the `CreateServerChain`\\n13: function in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go`.\\n14: \\n15: ```mermaid\\n16: graph TD\\n17:     subgraph Incoming Request\\n18:         direction LR\\n19:         A[User/Client] --> B{/apis/apps/v1/deployments};\\n20:     end\\n21: \\n22:     subgraph kube-apiserver process\\n23:         direction LR\\n24:         B --> C[Aggregator Server];\\n25:         C -- Not an APIService --> D[Kube API Server];\\n26:         D -- Handles Request --> E[REST Storage];\\n27:         C -- Is an APIService --> F[Proxy to Extension API Server];\\n28:         D -- Not a Core API --> G[API Extensions Server];\\n29:         G -- Handles CRD --> E;\\n30:     end\\n31: ```\\n32: \\n33: 1.  **Aggregator Server (`kube-aggregator`):**\\n34:     *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiregistration.k8s.io` API and acts as a reverse proxy for\\n35:         extension API servers. This functionality was designed to allow third-party APIs to be\\n36:         \\\"aggregated\\\" into the main Kubernetes API server seamlessly.\\n37:     *   **Mechanism:** It watches `APIService` objects. When a request arrives (e.g., for\\n38:         `/apis/mycompany.com/v1/myresources`), it checks if an `APIService` has \\\"claimed\\\"\\n39:         that path. If so, it uses a `ServiceResolver` to find the IP of the backing\\n40:         `Service` and proxies the request.\\n41:     *   **Use Case:** This pattern is for programmatic, high-control extensions that require\\n42:         custom business logic (e.g., non-CRUD subresources like `/logs`) or alternative\\n43:         storage backends.\\n44:     *   **Delegation:** If no `APIService` matches, it delegates the request to the next\\n45:         server in the chain.\\n46: \\n47: 2.  **Kube API Server (Core):**\\n48:     *   **Purpose:** Serves all the built-in Kubernetes APIs (`core/v1`, `apps/v1`, etc.).\\n49:     *   **Mechanism:** This is the main server, configured with all the core REST storage\\n50:         strategies.\\n51:     *   **Delegation:** If a request is for a path that is not a core API (e.g., for a CRD),\\n52:         it delegates the request to the next server in the chain.\\n53: \\n54: 3.  **API Extensions Server (`apiextensions-apiserver`):**\\n55:     *   **Purpose:** Handles the `apiextensions.k8s.io` API, which manages\\n56:         `CustomResourceDefinition` objects (CRDs). The evolution of CRDs from a simple extension\\n57:         mechanism to a feature-rich system with validation, versioning, and defaulting is\\n58:         documented in a series of KEPs, starting with the graduation to GA in Kubernetes v1.16.\\n59:     *   **Mechanism:** When a CRD is created, this server dynamically creates and installs a\\n60:         new REST storage handler for the new resource, making it immediately available.\\n61:     *   **Use Case:** CRDs are the most common extension pattern, offering a declarative,\\n62:         schema-based way to define new resource types that are stored in etcd and require no\\n63:         custom API server code.\\n64:     *   **Delegation:** It is the end of the chain. If it cannot handle a request, a `404 Not\\n65:         Found` is returned.\\n66: \\n67: ## 2. Handler Chain\\n68: \\n69: Every request flows through a standard chain of HTTP handlers (filters). The request body\\n70: is not deserialized until it has passed authentication and authorization. The default handler\\n71: chain is constructed by the `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` function in\\n72: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`.\\n73: \\n74: ```mermaid\\n75: sequenceDiagram\\n76:     participant Client\\n77:     participant Handler Chain\\n78:     participant Authentication\\n79:     participant Authorization\\n80:     participant Priority and Fairness\\n81:     participant Admission Control\\n82:     participant REST Endpoint\\n83: \\n84:     Client->>Handler Chain: Request\\n85:     Handler Chain->>Authentication: Authenticate\\n86:     Authentication-->>Handler Chain: User Info\\n87:     Handler Chain->>Authorization: Authorize\\n88:     Authorization-->>Handler Chain: Allowed/Denied\\n89:     Handler Chain->>Priority and Fairness: Classify & Queue\\n90:     Priority and Fairness-->>Handler Chain: Proceed\\n91:     Handler Chain->>Admission Control: Mutate & Validate\\n92:     Admission Control-->>Handler Chain: Object OK\\n93:     Handler Chain->>REST Endpoint: Handle\\n94:     REST Endpoint-->>Handler Chain: Response\\n95:     Handler Chain-->>Client: Response\\n96: ```\\n97: \\n98: The handler chain consists of the following stages:\\n99: \\n100: 1.  **Authentication (`pkg/authentication`):** This filter identifies the user. The system is\\n101:     pluggable and composed of multiple authenticators (e.g., client certs, bearer tokens, OIDC).\\n102:     The identity of the user is determined by the first authenticator in the chain that successfully\\n103:     identifies the user.\\n104: 2.  **Authorization (`pkg/authorization`):** This filter checks if the user is permitted to\\n105:     perform the action. This system is also pluggable and composed of multiple authorizers\\n106:     (e.g., RBAC, Node, Webhook). Each authorizer may respond with either allow, deny, or no opinion.\\n107:     If the response is no opinion, the request is passed to the next authorizer in the chain.\\n108: 3.  **Priority and Fairness (`pkg/util/flowcontrol`):** This subsystem manages request\\n109:     concurrency, classifying requests into `FlowSchema`s and `PriorityLevel`s to prevent\\n110:     overload. This feature was introduced to prevent high traffic from overwhelming the API\\n111:     server and to ensure that critical cluster operations are not starved.\\n112: 4.  **Admission Control (`pkg/admission`):** This is the primary mechanism for policy\\n113:     enforcement. It is only at this stage that the request body is deserialized into an\\n114:     object. It is a chain of plugins that can mutate or validate an object. The built-in Pod\\n115:     Security admission controller is a key example of this, enforcing Pod Security Standards\\n116:     at the namespace level.\\n117: 5.  **REST Endpoint Handling (`pkg/endpoints`):** The request is finally dispatched to the\\n118:     appropriate REST handler, which is installed by the `APIInstaller`.\\n119: \\n120: ## 3. API Group Registration\\n121: \\n122: The high-level steps for introducing an API are:\\n123: \\n124: 1.  **Define Types:** Create or modify the Go structs in the `types.go` file for the API group.\\n125: 2.  **Generate Code:** Use the code generators provided by the Kubernetes project to create the required\\n126:     boilerplate methods for deep-copy, conversion, and defaulting.\\n127: 3.  **Implement the `Strategy`:** Write the custom business logic and validation for the\\n128:     resource in its `Strategy` object.\\n129: 4.  **Register and Install:** Create the `APIGroupInfo` struct, bundling the `Scheme` and the\\n130:     `Strategy`-configured storage, and pass it to the `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup`\\n131:     method.\\n132: \\n133: ### The API Group Registry\\n134: \\n135: The `runtime.Scheme` acts as a central registry for an API group's type information. A single\\n136: `Scheme` object is created for each API group and is responsible for the following key\\n137: capabilities:\\n138: \\n139: *   **Type Registration and Mapping:** The `Scheme`'s primary role is to map a GroupVersionKind\\n140:     (GVK) to its corresponding Go type and back. This process also relies on the `deepcopy-gen`\\n141:     tool to create `DeepCopy()` methods for each type, which is critical for ensuring that\\n142:     objects returned from caches are never modified directly.\\n143: \\n144: *   **API Conversion:** The `Scheme` stores the conversion functions that translate objects\\n145:     between different API versions. These functions are typically generated by the\\n146:     `conversion-gen` tool and enable the **hub-and-spoke** model.\\n147: \\n148: *   **Defaulting:** The `Scheme` registers defaulting functions that populate optional fields in\\n149:     an object. These are usually generated by the `defaulter-gen` tool.\\n150: \\n151: *   **Declarative Validation:** The `Scheme` can store and execute code-generated validation\\n152:     functions, providing a baseline level of validation. This is distinct from the primary,\\n153:     handwritten business logic validation, which is handled by the `Strategy` object.\\n154: \\n155: ### The `APIGroupInfo` Struct and `Strategy` Object\\n156: \\n157: With a populated `Scheme`, the API group is registered with the `GenericAPIServer` by bundling\\n158: the `Scheme` with the storage backend and versioning information into an `APIGroupInfo` struct.\\n159: \\n160: ```mermaid\\n161: graph TD\\n162:     subgraph Server Configuration\\n163:         A[APIGroupInfo for apps v1];\\n164:         A --> B{Scheme: Knows Deployment v1};\\n165:         A --> C{Storage: deployments RESTStorage};\\n166:         A --> D{Version Priority: v1, v1beta1};\\n167:     end\\n168: \\n169:     subgraph RESTStorage Implementation\\n170:         C --> E[genericregistry.Store];\\n171:         E --> F[etcd client];\\n172:         E --> G[Deployment Strategy];\\n173:     end\\n174: \\n175:     subgraph Server Runtime\\n176:         H[GenericAPIServer] -- InstallAPIGroup --> I[APIInstaller];\\n177:         I -- Uses --> A;\\n178:         I --> J{Register /apis/apps/v1/deployments};\\n179:         J --> K[HTTP Handler];\\n180:         K -- On Request --> C;\\n181:     end\\n182: ```\\n183: \\n184: The registration process follows these steps:\\n185: \\n186: 1.  **`APIGroupInfo` Construction:** For each API group, an `APIGroupInfo` struct is created,\\n187:     which contains the populated `Scheme`, a map of resources to their storage\\n188:     implementations, and an ordered list of **Version Priority**.\\n189: \\n190: 2.  **REST Storage Instantiation:** For each resource, a `genericregistry.Store` is created. It\\n191:     is configured with a resource-specific `Strategy` object that contains the core business\\n192:     logic (e.g., handwritten validation).\\n193: \\n194: 3.  **API Group Installation:** The `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup` method takes the\\n195:     `APIGroupInfo` and uses an `APIInstaller` to expose the resources as HTTP endpoints.\\n196: \\n197: ## 4. Watch Cache\\n198: \\n199: To handle the high volume of watch requests from controllers without overwhelming etcd, the\\n200: apiserver uses a **watch cache**. The implementation can be found in\\n201: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/`.\\n202: \\n203: *   **Initialization:** The cacher first performs a `LIST` to get the current state of all\\n204:     objects and a `ResourceVersion` for that point-in-time. It then starts a `WATCH` from\\n205:     that version to ensure a consistent stream of events.\\n206: *   **Serving from Cache:** Most list and watch requests are served from this in-memory cache, which\\n207:     dramatically reduces the load on etcd. Consistent reads are also served from the\\n208:     cache. This is achieved by first fetching the revision number of the latest write from\\n209:     etcd. The server then ensures the cache is at least that recent\u2014waiting for it to\\n210:     refresh if necessary\u2014before serving the request.\\n211: *   **Fallback to Storage:** If a client request cannot be served from the\\n212:     cache's buffer, the request \\\"falls through\\\" to the underlying etcd storage.\\n213: *   **Bookmarks:** The cacher uses bookmark events to track the latest `ResourceVersion` for\\n214:     unchanged objects. This prevents the cache's `ResourceVersion` from becoming too old,\\n215:     which avoids the need for expensive relist operations from etcd when the objects have\\n216:     not been modified.\\n217: \\n218: ## 5. Conflict Resolution\\n219: \\n220: *   **Optimistic Concurrency via `resourceVersion`:** Clients are expected to perform updates using a\\n221:     read-modify-write workflow. The apiserver uses the `resourceVersion` field of every\\n222:     object to enforce optimistic concurrency. This `resourceVersion` is not an arbitrary number;\\n223:     it maps directly to etcd's globally consistent `mod_revision`. When a client submits an\\n224:     update (`PUT` or `PATCH`), it must provide the `resourceVersion` of the object it based its\\n225:     modifications on. If the `resourceVersion` on the server does not match the current\\n226:     `mod_revision` in etcd, the server rejects the request with a `409 Conflict` error. This\\n227:     forces the client to re-read the object, resolve the conflict, and resubmit with the new\\n228:     `resourceVersion`.\\n229: *   **Server-Side Apply:** A declarative, \\\"intent-based\\\" patch. The server maintains a\\n230:     `managedFields` section in the object's metadata to track which \\\"manager\\\" (e.g., a\\n231:     controller) owns each field. This allows multiple actors to manage different parts of the\\n232:     same object without overwriting each other's changes.\\n233: \\n234: ## 6. Discovery and OpenAPI\\n235: \\n236: Apiservers serve the `/apis` discovery endpoints and the `/openapi/v2` and `/openapi/v3`\\n237: specifications. The generation of the OpenAPI specification is a multi-stage process.\\n238: \\n239: *   **`openapi-gen`**: This tool reflects on Go structs, reads godoc comments, and looks at\\n240:     validation struct tags to generate a map of all API definitions.\\n241: *   **`zz_generated.openapi.go`**: The output is a large Go file containing a\\n242:     `GetOpenAPIDefinitions` function.\\n243: *   **Runtime**: The `GenericAPIServer` calls this generated function to build the final OpenAPI\\n244:     JSON spec that it serves to clients.\\n245: \\n246: ## 7. Security & Observability\\n247: \\n248: *   **Audit (`pkg/audit`):** The apiserver has a policy-driven event logging pipeline. The audit\\n249:     policy controls what is logged and at which stage of a request.\\n250: *   **Security:**\\n251:     *   **mTLS:** The primary authentication mechanism for system components.\\n252:     *   **Service Account Token Issuance:** The `kube-apiserver` acts as an OIDC provider,\\n253:         issuing and validating JWTs for `ServiceAccount`s.\\n254: \\n255: ## 8. Streaming Protocols\\n256: \\n257: *   **Websockets:** The apiserver uses websockets to upgrade HTTP\\n258:     connections for interactive, streaming protocols like `exec`, `attach`, and\\n259:     `port-forward`. The `UpgradeAwareProxyHandler` manages this process.\\n260: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes@c18ca078466118135fcab744ab3fe6e47c94a97d/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/ARCHITECTURE.md\"}",

If it cannot handle a request, a `404 Not\n65:         Found` is returned.\n66: \n67: ## 2. Handler Chain\n68: \n69: Every request flows through a standard chain of HTTP handlers (filters). The request body\n70: is not deserialized until it has passed authentication and authorization. The default handler\n71: chain is constructed by the `DefaultBuildHandlerChain` function in\n72: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/config.go`.\n73: \n74: ```mermaid\n75: sequenceDiagram\n76:     participant Client\n77:     participant Handler Chain\n78:     participant Authentication\n79:     participant Authorization\n80:     participant Priority and Fairness\n81:     participant Admission Control\n82:     participant REST Endpoint\n83: \n84:     Client->>Handler Chain: Request\n85:     Handler Chain->>Authentication: Authenticate\n86:     Authentication-->>Handler Chain: User Info\n87:     Handler Chain->>Authorization: Authorize\n88:     Authorization-->>Handler Chain: Allowed/Denied\n89:     Handler Chain->>Priority and Fairness: Classify & Queue\n90:     Priority and Fairness-->>Handler Chain: Proceed\n91:     Handler Chain->>Admission Control: Mutate & Validate\n92:     Admission Control-->>Handler Chain: Object OK\n93:     Handler Chain->>REST Endpoint: Handle\n94:     REST Endpoint-->>Handler Chain: Response\n95:     Handler Chain-->>Client: Response\n96: ```\n97: \n98: The handler chain consists of the following stages:\n99: \n100: 1.  **Authentication (`pkg/authentication`):** This filter identifies the user. The system is\n101:     pluggable and composed of multiple authenticators (e.g., client certs, bearer tokens, OIDC).\n102:     The identity of the user is determined by the first authenticator in the chain that successfully\n103:     identifies the user.\n104: 2.  **Authorization (`pkg/authorization`):** This filter checks if the user is permitted to\n105:     perform the action. This system is also pluggable and composed of multiple authorizers\n106:     (e.g., RBAC, Node, Webhook). Each authorizer may respond with either allow, deny, or no opinion.\n107:     If the response is no opinion, the request is passed to the next authorizer in the chain.\n108: 3.  **Priority and Fairness (`pkg/util/flowcontrol`):** This subsystem manages request\n109:     concurrency, classifying requests into `FlowSchema`s and `PriorityLevel`s to prevent\n110:     overload. This feature was introduced to prevent high traffic from overwhelming the API\n111:     server and to ensure that critical cluster operations are not starved.\n112: 4.  **Admission Control (`pkg/admission`):** This is the primary mechanism for policy\n113:     enforcement. It is only at this stage that the request body is deserialized into an\n114:     object. It is a chain of plugins that can mutate or validate an object. The built-in Pod\n115:     Security admission controller is a key example of this, enforcing Pod Security Standards\n116:     at the namespace level.\n117: 5.  **REST Endpoint Handling (`pkg/endpoints`):** The request is finally dispatched to the\n118:     appropriate REST handler, which is installed by the `APIInstaller`.\n119: \n120: ## 3. API Group Registration\n121: \n122: The high-level steps for introducing an API are:\n123: \n124: 1.  **Define Types:** Create or modify the Go structs in the `types.go` file for the API group.\n125: 2.  **Generate Code:** Use the code generators provided by the Kubernetes project to create the required\n126:     boilerplate methods for deep-copy, conversion, and defaulting.\n127: 3.  **Implement the `Strategy`:** Write the custom business logic and validation for the\n128:     resource in its `Strategy` object.\n129: 4.  **Register and Install:** Create the `APIGroupInfo` struct, bundling the `Scheme` and the\n130:     `Strategy`-configured storage, and pass it to the `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup`\n131:     method.\n132: \n133: ### The API Group Registry\n134: \n135: The `runtime.Scheme` acts as a central registry for an API group's type information. A single\n136: `Scheme` object is created for each API group and is responsible for the following key\n137: capabilities:\n138: \n139: *   **Type Registration and Mapping:** The `Scheme`'s primary role is to map a GroupVersionKind\n140:     (GVK) to its corresponding Go type and back. This process also relies on the `deepcopy-gen`\n141:     tool to create `DeepCopy()` methods for each type, which is critical for ensuring that\n142:     objects returned from caches are never modified directly.\n143: \n144: *   **API Conversion:** The `Scheme` stores the conversion functions that translate objects\n145:     between different API versions. These functions are typically generated by the\n146:     `conversion-gen` tool and enable the **hub-and-spoke** model.\n147: \n148: *   **Defaulting:** The `Scheme` registers defaulting functions that populate optional fields in\n149:     an object. These are usually generated by the `defaulter-gen` tool.\n150: \n151: *   **Declarative Validation:** The `Scheme` can store and execute code-generated validation\n152:     functions, providing a baseline level of validation. This is distinct from the primary,\n153:     handwritten business logic validation, which is handled by the `Strategy` object.\n154: \n155: ### The `APIGroupInfo` Struct and `Strategy` Object\n156: \n157: With a populated `Scheme`, the API group is registered with the `GenericAPIServer` by bundling\n158: the `Scheme` with the storage backend and versioning information into an `APIGroupInfo` struct.\n159: \n160: ```mermaid\n161: graph TD\n162:     subgraph Server Configuration\n163:         A[APIGroupInfo for apps v1];\n164:         A --> B{Scheme: Knows Deployment v1};\n165:         A --> C{Storage: deployments RESTStorage};\n166:         A --> D{Version Priority: v1, v1beta1};\n167:     end\n168: \n169:     subgraph RESTStorage Implementation\n170:         C --> E[genericregistry.Store];\n171:         E --> F[etcd client];\n172:         E --> G[Deployment Strategy];\n173:     end\n174: \n175:     subgraph Server Runtime\n176:         H[GenericAPIServer] -- InstallAPIGroup --> I[APIInstaller];\n177:         I -- Uses --> A;\n178:         I --> J{Register /apis/apps/v1/deployments};\n179:         J --> K[HTTP Handler];\n180:         K -- On Request --> C;\n181:     end\n182: ```\n183: \n184: The registration process follows these steps:\n185: \n186: 1.  **`APIGroupInfo` Construction:** For each API group, an `APIGroupInfo` struct is created,\n187:     which contains the populated `Scheme`, a map of resources to their storage\n188:     implementations, and an ordered list of **Version Priority**.\n189: \n190: 2.  **REST Storage Instantiation:** For each resource, a `genericregistry.Store` is created. It\n191:     is configured with a resource-specific `Strategy` object that contains the core business\n192:     logic (e.g., handwritten validation).\n193: \n194: 3.  **API Group Installation:** The `GenericAPIServer`'s `InstallAPIGroup` method takes the\n195:     `APIGroupInfo` and uses an `APIInstaller` to expose the resources as HTTP endpoints.\n196: \n197: ## 4. Watch Cache\n198: \n199: To handle the high volume of watch requests from controllers without overwhelming etcd, the\n200: apiserver uses a **watch cache**. The implementation can be found in\n201: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/cacher/`.\n202: \n203: *   **Initialization:** The cacher first performs a `LIST` to get the current state of all\n204:     objects and a `ResourceVersion` for that point-in-time. It then starts a `WATCH` from\n205:     that version to ensure a consistent stream of events.\n206: *   **Serving from Cache:** Most list and watch requests are served from this in-memory cache, which\n207:     dramatically reduces the load on etcd. Consistent reads are also served from the\n208:     cache. This is achieved by first fetching the revision number of the latest write from\n209:     etcd. The server then ensures the cache is at least that recent\u2014waiting for it to\n210:     refresh if necessary\u2014before serving the request.\n211: *   **Fallback to Storage:** If a client request cannot be served from the\n212:     cache's buffer, the request \"falls through\" to the underlying etcd storage.\n213: *   **Bookmarks:** The cacher uses bookmark events to track the latest `ResourceVersion` for\n214:     unchanged objects. This prevents the cache's `ResourceVersion` from becoming too old,\n215:     which avoids the need for expensive relist operations from etcd when the objects have\n216:     not been modified.\n217: \n218: ## 5. Conflict Resolution\n219: \n220: *   **Optimistic Concurrency via `resourceVersion`:** Clients are expected to perform updates using a\n221:     read-modify-write workflow. The apiserver uses the `resourceVersion` field of every\n222:     object to enforce optimistic concurrency. This `resourceVersion` is not an arbitrary number;\n223:     it maps directly to etcd's globally consistent `mod_revision`. When a client submits an\n224:     update (`PUT` or `PATCH`), it must provide the `resourceVersion` of the object it based its\n225:     modifications on. If the `resourceVersion` on the server does not match the current\n226:     `mod_revision` in etcd, the server rejects the request with a `409 Conflict` error. This\n227:     forces the client to re-read the object, resolve the conflict, and resubmit with the new\n228:     `resourceVersion`.\n229: *   **Server-Side Apply:** A declarative, \"intent-based\" patch. The server maintains a\n230:     `managedFields` section in the object's metadata to track which \"manager\" (e.g., a\n231:     controller) owns each field. This allows multiple actors to manage different parts of the\n232:     same object without overwriting each other's changes.\n233: \n234: ## 6. Discovery and OpenAPI\n235: \n236: Apiservers serve the `/apis` discovery endpoints and the `/openapi/v2` and `/openapi/v3`\n237: specifications. The generation of the OpenAPI specification is a multi-stage process.\n238: \n239: *   **`openapi-gen`**: This tool reflects on Go structs, reads godoc comments, and looks at\n240:     validation struct tags to generate a map of all API definitions.\n241: *   **`zz_generated.openapi.go`**: The output is a large Go file containing a\n242:     `GetOpenAPIDefinitions` function.\n243: *   **Runtime**: The `GenericAPIServer` calls this generated function to build the final OpenAPI\n244:     JSON spec that it serves to clients.\n245: \n246: ## 7. Security & Observability\n247: \n248: *   **Audit (`pkg/audit`):** The apiserver has a policy-driven event logging pipeline. The audit\n249:     policy controls what is logged and at which stage of a request.\n250: *   **Security:**\n251:     *   **mTLS:** The primary authentication mechanism for system components.\n252:     *   **Service Account Token Issuance:** The `kube-apiserver` acts as an OIDC provider,\n253:         issuing and validating JWTs for `ServiceAccount`s.\n254: \n255: ## 8. Streaming Protocols\n256: \n257: *   **Websockets:** The apiserver uses websockets to upgrade HTTP\n258:     connections for interactive, streaming protocols like `exec`, `attach`, and\n259:     `port-forward`. The `UpgradeAwareProxyHandler` manages this process.\n260: ",
    "url": "https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes@c18ca078466118135fcab744ab3fe6e47c94a97d/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/ARCHITECTURE.md"
  }
}

{
  "content": "# Kubernetes API Server Architecture and Extension Guide\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\nThe Kubernetes apiserver library (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver`) is a generic framework for building Kubernetes-compatible API servers. It provides the complete request handling infrastructure needed to expose resources as HTTP endpoints with authentication, authorization, admission control, and storage.\n\n**Primary Purpose:**\n- Offer a reusable library for building aggregated API servers (primary consumers: kube-apiserver core, API Extensions for CRDs, kube-aggregator for third-party APIs)\n- Handle the full HTTP request lifecycle: authentication \u2192 authorization \u2192 admission \u2192 REST operations \u2192 response\n- Manage concurrent requests with fairness and priority\n- Provide storage abstraction for multiple backends\n- Enforce Kubernetes API semantics (versioning, resource versions, watch semantics)\n\n**Upstream Dependencies:**\n- `apimachinery` - Type definitions, runtime, serialization, and generic utilities\n- `client-go` - Client libraries and informers\n- `component-base` - Shared components (metrics, logs, feature gates)\n- `kube-openapi` - OpenAPI spec generation\n\n**Downstream Consumers:**\n- `kube-apiserver` (main Kubernetes API server)\n- `apiextensions-apiserver` (custom resource definitions)\n- `kube-aggregator` (extension API servers)\n- Third-party API servers built with this library\n\n**Scope Boundaries:**\n- Does NOT include: Storage backends (etcd is pluggable), container runtime, node-level operations\n- Includes: Request filtering, middleware chain, storage abstraction, REST endpoint registry, audit logging, watch caching\n- Intentionally generic: Makes no assumptions about specific resource types or business logic\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Division\n\n### 2.1 Core Server Architecture\n\n#### GenericAPIServer (`pkg/server/genericapiserver.go`)\n**Responsibility:** Central orchestrator for the API server lifecycle and resource registration.\n\nKey responsibilities:\n- Initialize HTTP handler chain via `DefaultBuildHandlerChain`\n- Register API groups and resources via `InstallAPIGroup(s)`\n- Manage OpenAPI/discovery endpoints\n- Maintain storage backends and lifecycle hooks (PostStart, PreShutdown)\n- Expose `/healthz`, `/livez`, `/readyz` readiness checks\n\n**Critical Methods:**\n- `InstallAPIGroup(apiGroupInfo *APIGroupInfo) error` - Registers a new API group with versioning, discovery, and storage\n- `PrepareRun()` - Finalizes configuration before serving (generates OpenAPI specs, validates configuration)\n- `Run(stopCh <-chan struct{}) error` - Starts the HTTP server\n\n---\n\n### 2.2 Handler Chain and Request Filtering\n\n#### Handler Chain Pipeline (`pkg/server/config.go:DefaultBuildHandlerChain`)\n**Responsibility:** Orchestrate layered HTTP middleware filters for request processing.\n\nThe handler chain processes requests in this order (outermost to innermost):\n\n1. **Audit Init** - Initialize audit context\n2. **Panic Recovery** - Catch and log panics\n3. **Request Info** - Parse request URL to extract resource/verb/namespace info\n4. **Received Timestamp** - Record when request was received\n5. **Mux & Discovery Complete** - Block requests if server still initializing\n6. **Latency Tracking** - Measure filter processing time\n7. **Max In-Flight Limit** - Concurrency control (or Priority & Fairness if enabled)\n8. **Impersonation** - Allow privileged users to act as other identities\n9. **Audit** - Log request details per audit policy\n10. **Authentication** - Identify the user (client certs, bearer tokens, OIDC, etc.)\n11. **Authorization** - Check if user can perform the action\n12. **Priority & Fairness** - Classify requests and enforce flow control\n13. **Request Deadline** - Set timeout for request processing\n14. **Timeout for Non-Long-Running** - Timeout short requests\n15. **Cache Control** - Add HTTP cache directives\n16. **REST Handler** - Delegate to actual resource handler\n\n**Filter Packages:**\n- `pkg/endpoints/filters/` - Authentication, authorization, audit, warning headers, request deadline\n- `pkg/server/filters/` - CORS, HSTS, timeout, priority/fairness, max in-flight, panic recovery\n\n---\n\n### 2.3 Endpoint Installation and REST Handlers\n\n#### APIInstaller (`pkg/endpoints/installer.go`)\n**Responsibility:** Register HTTP endpoints for each resource and configure REST operations.\n\n**Process:**\n1. Takes `APIGroupInfo` containing schema, versioning, and storage implementations\n2. Introspects storage to determine available operations (GET, LIST, POST, DELETE, PATCH, WATCH)\n3. For each resource, registers HTTP routes using go-restful\n4. Configures request/response serialization negotiation\n5. Attaches scope namers for URL parsing (cluster-scoped vs namespace-scoped)\n\n**Handler Functions** (`pkg/endpoints/handlers/`):\n- `create.go` - POST handler for creating resources\n- `get.go` - GET handler for retrieving resources\n- `delete.go` - DELETE handler with grace period and cascading options\n- `update.go` - PUT handler for full object replacement\n- `patch.go` - PATCH handler for partial updates (JSON Patch, Merge Patch, Server-Side Apply)\n- `watch.go` - GET handler with `watch=true` query parameter for streaming events\n- `rest.go` - Core REST request scope and handler utilities\n\n---\n\n### 2.4 Admission Control\n\n#### Admission Chain (`pkg/admission/`)\n**Responsibility:** Enforce policy on objects before storage (mutation and validation).\n\n**Key Concepts:**\n- Admission happens AFTER authorization but BEFORE object is written to storage\n- Runs only on write operations (CREATE, UPDATE, PATCH, DELETE)\n- Separated into two phases: Mutating (can modify object) \u2192 Validating (read-only checks)\n\n**Built-in Plugins:**\n- `ValidatingWebhook` - Call external webhooks for validation\n- `MutatingWebhook` - Call external webhooks for mutation\n- `ValidatingAdmissionPolicy` - CEL-based validation rules\n- `MutatingAdmissionPolicy` - CEL-based mutation rules\n- `NamespaceLifecycle` - Prevent deletion of non-empty namespaces\n\n**Interfaces** (`pkg/admission/interfaces.go`):\n```go\nInterface        // Main admission controller interface\nValidationInterface  // Validation-only handlers\nMutationInterface    // Mutation-only handlers\n```\n\n**Chain Execution:**\nConfigured as a chain of handlers. Request passes through all handlers; any handler can reject with an error or mutate the object.\n\n---\n\n### 2.5 Authentication\n\n#### Authenticators (`pkg/authentication/`)\n**Responsibility:** Identify who is making the request and extract user information.\n\n**Authenticator Types:**\n- `x509` - Client certificate validation\n- `bearer_token` - Bearer token validation (ServiceAccount tokens, OIDC, etc.)\n- `basic_auth` - HTTP basic authentication\n- `token` - Generic token authenticators\n- `request_header` - Extract identity from request headers (used by aggregator)\n- `union` - Chain multiple authenticators; first to succeed wins\n\n**Output:** `user.Info` struct containing:\n- UID (unique identifier)\n- Name (username)\n- Groups (group memberships)\n- Extra (additional attributes)\n\n**Configuration:** Pluggable via `AuthenticationInfo` in `Config`\n\n---\n\n### 2.6 Authorization\n\n#### Authorizers (`pkg/authorization/`)\n**Responsibility:** Decide if an authenticated user can perform an action.\n\n**Authorizer Types:**\n- `RBAC` - Role-based access control via Role/ClusterRole/Binding resources\n- `Node` - Special authorization for kubelets\n- `ABAC` - Attribute-based access control\n- `Webhook` - External authorization webhooks\n- `union` - Chain multiple authorizers; first definitive decision wins (Allow/Deny), or pass to next\n\n**Decision Outcomes:**\n- Allow - User is authorized\n- Deny - User is forbidden\n- No Opinion - Next authorizer in chain decides\n\n**Attributes Passed:**\n- User info (from authentication)\n- HTTP method and path\n- Namespace and resource\n- Verb (get, list, create, update, patch, delete, watch, etc.)\n\n**Configuration:** Pluggable via `AuthorizationInfo` in `Config`\n\n---\n\n### 2.7 Storage Abstraction Layer\n\n#### Storage Interface (`pkg/storage/interfaces.go`)\n**Responsibility:** Abstract storage backend operations (etcd, in-memory cache, etc.).\n\n**Key Interfaces:**\n- `Interface` - Core storage operations (Create, Delete, Get, List, Watch, GuaranteedUpdate)\n- `Versioner` - Manage resource versions (etcd `mod_revision` mapping)\n- `Storage` - Metadata and type information\n- `Cacher` - In-memory watch cache for LIST/WATCH performance\n\n**Storage Implementations:**\n- `storage/etcd3/` - etcd v3 backend (primary production backend)\n- `storage/cacher/` - Layered watch cache to reduce etcd load\n- `storage/testing/` - Mock storage for testing\n\n#### RESTStorage (`pkg/registry/rest/storage.go`)\n**Responsibility:** Bridge between HTTP handlers and storage backend.\n\n**Key Operations:**\n- `Get(ctx, name)` - Retrieve single resource\n- `List(ctx, options)` - List resources with filtering, pagination, label selection\n- `Create(ctx, obj)` - Create new resource\n- `Update(ctx, name, objInfo)` - Replace entire resource\n- `Delete(ctx, name)` - Delete resource with grace period\n- `Watch(ctx, options)` - Stream events for resource changes\n\n#### Watch Cache (`pkg/storage/cacher/`)\n**Responsibility:** In-memory cache of resources to handle watch requests without overwhelming etcd.\n\n**Mechanism:**\n1. Perform initial LIST to get current state and `resourceVersion`\n2. Start WATCH from that version\n3. Serve subsequent LIST/WATCH requests from cache when consistent\n4. Fall through to storage if cache cannot serve the request (too old, missing data)\n5. Use bookmark events to maintain recent `resourceVersion`\n\n**Benefit:** Dramatically reduces etcd load from watch requests\n\n---\n\n### 2.8 API Group Registration\n\n#### APIGroupInfo (`pkg/server/genericapiserver.go`)\n**Responsibility:** Bundle version information, storage, and schema for an API group.\n\n**Contents:**\n- `PrioritizedVersions` - Ordered list of versions (first is preferred)\n- `VersionedResourcesStorageMap` - Storage implementations per version/resource\n- `Scheme` - Runtime type registry with serialization, conversion, defaulting\n- `NegotiatedSerializer` - Protocol negotiation (JSON, protobuf, YAML)\n- `ParameterCodec` - Convert query parameters to Go types\n\n**Registration Process:**\n1. Define API types (Go structs)\n2. Register types in `Scheme`\n3. Implement `Strategy` with business logic and validation\n4. Create `genericregistry.Store` with Strategy and storage backend\n5. Build `APIGroupInfo` with versioned storage map\n6. Call `GenericAPIServer.InstallAPIGroup(apiGroupInfo)`\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow with Concrete Evidence\n\nThis section traces a sample request (`GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments/nginx`) through the entire system.\n\n### 3.1 Request Reception and Handler Chain\n\n**Entry Point:** `pkg/server/config.go:DefaultBuildHandlerChain` wraps the API handler with filters.\n\n**Flow:**\n```\nHTTP Request\n  \u2193\n[Audit Init]  pkg/endpoints/filters/audit_init.go\n  \u2193\n[Panic Recovery]  pkg/server/filters/wrap.go:WithPanicRecovery\n  \u2193\n[Request Info]  pkg/endpoints/filters/requestinfo.go\n  - Extracts: namespace=\"default\", resource=\"deployments\", verb=\"get\", name=\"nginx\"\n  - Stores in request context\n  \u2193\n[Received Timestamp]  pkg/endpoints/filters/request_received_time.go\n  - Records when request arrived for latency tracking\n  \u2193\n[Mux & Discovery Complete]  pkg/endpoints/filters/mux_discovery_complete.go\n  - Blocks if server still initializing\n  \u2193\n[Max In-Flight Limit]  pkg/server/filters/maxinflight.go:WithMaxInFlightLimit\n  - Rate-limits concurrent requests if necessary\n  \u2193\n[Impersonation]  pkg/endpoints/filters/impersonation/impersonation.go\n  - Checks if user is allowed to impersonate another user\n  \u2193\n[Audit]  pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go\n  - Logs request details based on audit policy\n  \u2193\n[Authentication]  pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go:WithAuthentication\n  - Runs authenticator chain (client cert, bearer token, OIDC, etc.)\n  - Identifies user, extracts groups\n  \u2193\n[Authorization]  pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go:WithAuthorization\n  - Runs authorizer chain (RBAC, Node, Webhook)\n  - Checks if user can GET deployments in namespace \"default\"\n  \u2193\n[REST Handler]  pkg/endpoints/handlers/get.go:GetResource\n```\n\n### 3.2 Storage Lookup and Deserialization\n\n**REST Handler Entry Point:** `pkg/endpoints/handlers/rest.go`\n\n**Process:**\n1. Extract resource info from request context (namespace, name, version)\n2. Select appropriate storage backend from `APIGroupInfo.VersionedResourcesStorageMap`\n3. Call storage `Get(ctx, \"default/nginx\")` to retrieve from etcd or cache\n\n**Storage Flow:**\n```\nREST Handler calls storage.Get()\n  \u2193\n[Cacher/Storage Layer]  pkg/storage/cacher/caching_object.go\n  - Check if object is in watch cache (if enabled)\n  - Cache hit? Return cached object\n  - Cache miss? Fall through to etcd\n  \u2193\n[etcd3 Storage]  pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go\n  - Query etcd: GET /registry/deployments/default/nginx\n  - Decode raw bytes to Go object\n  \u2193\n[Versioner]  pkg/storage/api_object_versioner.go\n  - Extract etcd mod_revision \u2192 set ResourceVersion field\n  \u2193\nReturn object to REST handler\n```\n\n### 3.3 Serialization and Response\n\n**Response Handler:** `pkg/endpoints/handlers/response.go`\n\n**Process:**\n1. Determine requested media type (JSON, protobuf, YAML via content-type negotiation)\n2. Convert object to requested format\n3. Set HTTP headers (Content-Type, ETag, Cache-Control)\n4. Write response to client\n\n**Code Path:**\n```\nREST Handler formats response\n  \u2193\n[Serialization]  apimachinery/runtime/serializer/\n  - Use negotiated serializer to encode object\n  - Standard format: JSON marshaled object with metadata\n  \u2193\n[Response Writers]  pkg/endpoints/handlers/responsewriters/\n  - Wrap response with HTTP headers\n  - Add etag for caching\n  \u2193\nHTTP 200 OK\nContent-Type: application/json\nContent-Length: ...\n\n{\n  \"apiVersion\": \"apps/v1\",\n  \"kind\": \"Deployment\",\n  \"metadata\": {...},\n  \"spec\": {...},\n  \"status\": {...}\n}\n```\n\n### 3.4 Watch Request Flow (Streaming)\n\nFor requests with `?watch=true`:\n\n**Handler:** `pkg/endpoints/handlers/watch.go`\n\n**Process:**\n```\nREST Handler with watch=true\n  \u2193\n[Deserialize List Options]\n  - Extract: selector, timeout, resourceVersion\n  \u2193\n[Storage Watch]  pkg/storage/cacher/caching_watcher.go\n  - If resourceVersion provided: Watch from that point\n  - If not provided: Start from current and watch forward\n  \u2193\n[Streaming Response]\n  - HTTP 200 with Transfer-Encoding: chunked\n  - Upgrade connection to watch protocol\n  - Stream events as they arrive: ADDED, MODIFIED, DELETED\n  \u2193\n[Bookmark Events]  (keep resourceVersion fresh)\n  - Periodic bookmark events to prevent stale watches\n  - Helps clients reconnect without re-listing entire collection\n```\n\n### 3.5 Write Operation (POST Create)\n\nFor `POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments`:\n\n**Handler:** `pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go:CreateResource`\n\n**Flow:**\n```\n[Deserialization]\n  - Decode request body to Deployment object\n  - Set resourceVersion=\"\" (new object)\n  \u2193\n[Defaulting]  pkg/admission/\n  - Scheme applies registered defaulting functions\n  - Fill in default values (e.g., replicas=1)\n  \u2193\n[Mutating Admission]  pkg/admission/\n  - Run webhook/policy mutating controllers\n  - Can modify object (e.g., inject sidecar)\n  \u2193\n[Validating Admission]  pkg/admission/\n  - Run webhook/policy validating controllers\n  - Reject if object invalid\n  \u2193\n[Strategic Merge]  (for updates)\n  - Merge user's changes with existing managed fields\n  \u2193\n[Storage Create]  pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go\n  - Assign UID\n  - Set resourceVersion=1 (first version)\n  - etcd PUT /registry/deployments/default/nginx <object>\n  \u2193\n[Cache Invalidation]  pkg/storage/cacher/\n  - Update watch cache\n  - Notify watchers of ADDED event\n  \u2193\nHTTP 201 Created\nContent-Location: /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments/nginx\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Request Concurrency and Fairness\n\n**Failure Mode:** Thundering herd - one user's workload starves all others.\n\n**Mitigation:** Flow Control (`pkg/util/flowcontrol/`)\n- Classify requests into FlowSchemas (e.g., \"system:masters\" \u2192 PriorityLevel=system)\n- Queue requests per priority level with token buckets\n- Reject requests if queue full (429 Too Many Requests)\n- Ensures critical system operations can always make progress\n\n**Configuration:**\n- `MaxRequestsInFlight` - Limit parallel reads\n- `MaxMutatingRequestsInFlight` - Limit parallel writes\n- Or use `FlowControl` interface for more sophisticated priority scheduling\n\n**Tradeoff:** Flow control adds latency; disabled by default for backward compatibility.\n\n### 4.2 Watch Cache and Consistency\n\n**Failure Mode:** Watch cache lag \u2192 client sees stale data; expensive relist on reconnect.\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Maintain in-memory cache of all objects per resource\n- Use etcd mod_revision for consistency checking\n- Serve LIST from cache only if cache is \"recent enough\"\n- Emit bookmark events periodically to prevent resourceVersion drift\n- Fall back to etcd if cache cannot serve request\n\n**Limits:**\n- Cache holds entire resource collection in memory (trade RAM for etcd load reduction)\n- Bookmark interval configurable to balance memory vs. freshness\n\n**Code:** `pkg/storage/cacher/caching_object.go`\n\n### 4.3 Request Timeouts and Resource Limits\n\n**Failure Mode:** Long-running operations hang server; OOM from unbounded allocation.\n\n**Mitigations:**\n- `RequestTimeout` - Overall timeout for non-long-running requests (default 1 minute)\n- `MinRequestTimeout` - Minimum allowable timeout\n- `MaxRequestBodyBytes` - Reject oversized payloads\n- `JSONPatchMaxCopyBytes` - Limit JSON patch copy operations\n- Long-running request detection (`LongRunningFunc`) - Exempt watch/exec/logs\n\n**Code:** `pkg/server/filters/timeout.go`\n\n### 4.4 Optimistic Concurrency and Conflict Resolution\n\n**Failure Mode:** Lost updates - multiple clients edit same object.\n\n**Mitigation:** Optimistic locking via `resourceVersion`\n- Each object has `resourceVersion` = etcd `mod_revision`\n- Client must provide matching `resourceVersion` in update/patch\n- Server rejects if `resourceVersion` mismatch \u2192 409 Conflict\n- Forces client to retry: read \u2192 modify \u2192 write\n\n**Alternative:** Server-Side Apply\n- Clients declare \"fields I manage\" in `managedFields`\n- Server deduplicates concurrent updates by field ownership\n- Eliminates need for client retry loops\n\n**Code:** `pkg/storage/etcd3/store.go`, `pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/`\n\n### 4.5 Admission Control Latency\n\n**Failure Mode:** Webhook admission hangs \u2192 all creates/updates block.\n\n**Mitigations:**\n- Timeout per webhook (configurable, default 30s)\n- `FailurePolicy: Fail` or `FailurePolicy: Ignore` to decide on webhook error\n- Async policies can handle failures gracefully\n- Monitoring: metrics track webhook latency\n\n**Risk:** Webhooks are trusted code; malicious/buggy webhook can DoS API server.\n\n### 4.6 etcd Overload\n\n**Failure Mode:** etcd becomes unavailable \u2192 API server can read from cache but cannot write.\n\n**Current Status:**\n- Write operations fail with \"etcd unavailable\" error\n- Read operations may succeed from cache if `resourceVersion` <= cache's version\n- No automatic failover (would require multi-master etcd cluster)\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Watch cache reduces etcd load from LIST/WATCH (primary source of load)\n- Caching for reads via storageVersion consistency checks\n- Priority & Fairness prevents overload amplification\n\n### 4.7 Storage Transformation (Encryption) Overhead\n\n**Failure Mode:** Encryption/decryption is CPU-intensive; can bottleneck throughput.\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Encryption happens in-memory before etcd I/O\n- Uses `ResourceTransformers` interface for pluggable encryption\n- Can be disabled if not needed\n\n**Code:** `pkg/server/config.go` - `ResourceTransformers` field\n\n### 4.8 Discovery and OpenAPI Overhead\n\n**Failure Mode:** Large cluster with many CRDs \u2192 OpenAPI spec generation becomes slow.\n\n**Mitigations:**\n- OpenAPI spec generated at startup via reflection and code-gen tooling\n- Spec cached in memory\n- Can be disabled with `EnableDiscovery: false`\n\n**Tradeoff:** Large spec impacts client download/parsing performance\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 5.1 Authentication\n\n**Extension Point:** `Config.Authentication.Authenticator`\n\n**How to Extend:**\n```go\nimport \"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authentication/authenticator\"\n\ntype CustomAuthenticator struct{}\n\nfunc (ca *CustomAuthenticator) AuthenticateToken(ctx context.Context, token string) (*authenticator.Response, bool, error) {\n    // Validate token and return user info\n    return &authenticator.Response{\n        User: &user.DefaultInfo{\n            Name: \"custom-user\",\n            UID:  \"uid-123\",\n        },\n    }, true, nil\n}\n```\n\nPlug via `Config.Authentication.Authenticator`.\n\n**Risks:**\n- Broken authenticator \u2192 all requests fail (no one can authenticate)\n- Slow authenticator \u2192 API server becomes unresponsive\n- Should implement timeout and fallback behavior\n\n**Reference Implementation:** `pkg/authentication/authenticatorfactory/` shows how kube-apiserver wires authenticators.\n\n---\n\n### 5.2 Authorization\n\n**Extension Point:** `Config.Authorization.Authorizer`\n\n**How to Extend:**\n```go\nimport \"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/authorization/authorizer\"\n\ntype CustomAuthorizer struct{}\n\nfunc (ca *CustomAuthorizer) Authorize(ctx context.Context, a authorizer.Attributes) (authorizer.Decision, string, error) {\n    // Implement custom logic\n    if a.GetUser().GetName() == \"admin\" {\n        return authorizer.DecisionAllow, \"admin allowed\", nil\n    }\n    return authorizer.DecisionNoOpinion, \"\", nil // Next authorizer decides\n}\n```\n\n**Composition Pattern:** Multiple authorizers can be chained; first authoritative decision wins.\n\n**Risks:**\n- Denying legitimate requests \u2192 breaks cluster operations\n- Allowing illegitimate requests \u2192 security breach\n- Slow authorizer \u2192 affects all requests (runs on every API call)\n\n---\n\n### 5.3 Admission Control\n\n**Extension Point:** `Config.AdmissionControl` (admission chain interface)\n\n**Two Patterns:**\n\n**Pattern 1: Built-in Plugins**\nRegister your plugin in `pkg/admission/plugin/` and call it from `RegisterAllAdmissionPlugins()`.\n\n```go\n// pkg/admission/plugin/myplugin/admission.go\ntype Plugin struct{}\n\nfunc (p *Plugin) Admit(ctx context.Context, a admission.Attributes, o admission.ObjectInterfaces) error {\n    // Mutate or validate object\n    obj := a.GetObject()\n    // ... modify obj if needed ...\n    return nil // Allow, or return error to reject\n}\n\nfunc (p *Plugin) ValidateInitialization() error {\n    return nil\n}\n\nfunc Register(plugins *admission.Plugins) {\n    plugins.Register(\"MyPlugin\", func(config io.Reader) (admission.Interface, error) {\n        return &Plugin{}, nil\n    })\n}\n```\n\n**Pattern 2: Webhooks**\nDefine ValidatingWebhookConfiguration or MutatingWebhookConfiguration resources; apiserver calls external webhooks for each request.\n\n**Risks:**\n- Slow webhook \u2192 serializes all writes (admission runs on every write)\n- Broken webhook \u2192 blocks all creates/updates to namespace/resource\n- Webhook can mutate objects unexpectedly \u2192 data corruption\n\n---\n\n### 5.4 RESTStorage Implementation\n\n**Extension Point:** Pluggable storage backends via `genericregistry.Store`\n\n**How to Extend:**\n```go\nimport \"k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic\"\n\n// Create a custom storage\nstore := &genericregistry.Store{\n    NewFunc:     func() runtime.Object { return &MyResource{} },\n    NewListFunc: func() runtime.Object { return &MyResourceList{} },\n    Storage:     etcd3Storage, // Inject storage backend\n    Strategy:    myStrategy,   // Custom business logic\n}\n\n// Register in APIGroupInfo\napiGroupInfo.VersionedResourcesStorageMap[\"v1\"][\"myresources\"] = store\n```\n\n**Key Hooks:**\n- `Strategy.AllowCreateOnUpdate()` - Allow PUT to create\n- `Strategy.AllowUnconditionalUpdate()` - Allow update without resourceVersion\n- `Strategy.Canonicalize()` - Normalize object representation\n- `Strategy.ValidateUpdate()` - Business logic validation\n\n**Complexity:** Medium. Requires understanding of Kubernetes object model (metadata, specs, status).\n\n---\n\n### 5.5 Handler Chain Customization\n\n**Extension Point:** `Config.BuildHandlerChainFunc`\n\nOverride the entire handler chain for custom filtering.\n\n```go\nfunc CustomBuildHandlerChain(apiHandler http.Handler, c *genericapiserver.Config) http.Handler {\n    handler := apiHandler\n\n    // Wrap with custom filters\n    handler = MyCustomFilter(handler)\n    handler = genericapiserver.DefaultBuildHandlerChain(handler, c)\n\n    return handler\n}\n\nconfig.BuildHandlerChainFunc = CustomBuildHandlerChain\n```\n\n**Risks:**\n- Easy to accidentally remove security filters (authentication, authorization)\n- Must maintain handler ordering invariants\n\n**Reference:** See `pkg/server/config.go:DefaultBuildHandlerChain` for current filter order.\n\n---\n\n### 5.6 Request Info Resolution\n\n**Extension Point:** `Config.RequestInfoResolver`\n\nCustomize how requests are parsed (namespace, resource, verb extraction).\n\n```go\ntype CustomResolver struct{}\n\nfunc (cr *CustomResolver) NewRequestInfo(req *http.Request) (*request.RequestInfo, error) {\n    // Parse custom URL schemes or patterns\n    ri := &request.RequestInfo{\n        Verb:      \"get\",\n        Resource:  \"myresources\",\n        Namespace: \"default\",\n    }\n    return ri, nil\n}\n```\n\n**Use Case:** Custom URL schemes, kubelet requests with special `/api/v1/nodes/:nodeName/...` paths.\n\n---\n\n### 5.7 Post-Start Hooks\n\n**Extension Point:** `GenericAPIServer.AddPostStartHook(name, fn)`\n\nRun initialization code after server starts serving requests.\n\n```go\nserver.AddPostStartHook(\"my-plugin-init\", func(ctx PostStartHookContext) error {\n    // Initialize custom controllers, watchers, etc.\n    // Can use loopback client from ctx.LoopbackClientConfig\n    return nil\n})\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Initialize controllers\n- Warm up caches\n- Register sub-resources dynamically\n\n**Guarantee:** Hooks execute after server listens but before /healthz reports ready.\n\n**Risks:** Failing hook \u2192 server never becomes ready.\n\n---\n\n### 5.8 Pre-Shutdown Hooks\n\n**Extension Point:** `GenericAPIServer.AddPreShutdownHook(name, fn)`\n\nRun cleanup code before server stops.\n\n```go\nserver.AddPreShutdownHook(\"cleanup\", func() error {\n    // Drain requests, close connections\n    return nil\n})\n```\n\n**Use Cases:**\n- Graceful shutdown of controllers\n- Connection draining\n- Resource cleanup\n\n---\n\n### 5.9 Storage Backend Pluggability\n\n**Extension Point:** Implement custom `storage.Interface`\n\n```go\ntype CustomStorage struct {}\n\nfunc (cs *CustomStorage) Create(ctx context.Context, key string, obj, out runtime.Object, ttl *uint64, dryRun bool) error {\n    // Store object in custom backend\n    return nil\n}\n\n// Implement all other Interface methods...\n```\n\nThen wire into `RESTOptionsGetter.GetRESTOptions()`.\n\n**Complexity:** High. Must implement all storage operations (Create, Delete, Get, List, Watch, Update, GuaranteedUpdate).\n\n**Production Examples:** etcd3 backend in `pkg/storage/etcd3/`\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications and Performance Considerations\n\n### 6.1 Memory Usage\n\n**Primary Consumer:** Watch cache (`pkg/storage/cacher/`)\n- Stores entire resource collection per cache partition\n- For large clusters (10k+ objects): Cache can consume GBs of RAM\n- Can disable via feature gate if memory-constrained\n\n**Secondary Consumer:** OpenAPI spec\n- Cached spec for all API groups can be 10+ MB\n- Loaded entirely on startup\n\n**Tuning:** Monitor memory usage; adjust `MaxInMemoryResponseBytes`, disable features not needed.\n\n### 6.2 Latency Profile\n\n**Bottlenecks (in order of typical impact):**\n1. **Authentication/Authorization** - Runs on every request\n   - Service account token validation: sub-millisecond (cached)\n   - OIDC token validation: 100+ ms (external call)\n   - RBAC evaluation: 1-10ms depending on role complexity\n\n2. **Admission Webhooks** - Runs on all writes\n   - Usually 50-200ms per webhook\n   - Serialized (one webhook completes before next starts)\n   - Can be optimized with failure policy = Ignore\n\n3. **Storage Operations** - etcd latency\n   - Local etcd cluster: 1-5ms\n   - Remote etcd (non-local): 10-50ms\n   - Heavy writes: can degrade to 100+ms\n\n4. **Serialization** - Converting objects to JSON/protobuf\n   - Usually sub-millisecond\n   - Large objects (e.g., 1MB ConfigMap) can add 10+ms\n\n**P99 Tail Latencies:** Often 10-100x higher than median due to GC pauses, context switches.\n\n### 6.3 Throughput Limits\n\n**Typical Capacities (single apiserver instance):**\n- **Reads:** 5,000-10,000 requests/sec\n- **Writes:** 1,000-2,000 requests/sec\n- **Watch connections:** 10,000+ (limited by memory/file descriptors)\n\n**Limiting Factors:**\n- etcd throughput (worst case: 100s of writes/sec)\n- Admission webhook latency (serialized)\n- TLS handshake overhead for new connections\n- Network bandwidth\n\n**Scaling Pattern:** Run multiple apiservers; clients load-balance across replicas.\n\n### 6.4 Graceful Shutdown\n\n**Sequence:**\n1. Stop accepting new requests (`readyz` returns false)\n2. Drain in-flight requests up to `ShutdownTimeout`\n3. Close watch connections gracefully\n4. Stop server listeners\n5. Run PreShutdownHooks\n\n**Tuning:**\n- `ShutdownDelayDuration` - Wait before draining (allow load balancer to update)\n- `ShutdownWatchTerminationGracePeriod` - How long to wait for watches\n- `ShutdownTimeout` - Hard timeout for drain\n\n### 6.5 Observability\n\n**Key Metrics:**\n- `apiserver_request_duration_seconds` - Request latency by verb/resource\n- `apiserver_request_total` - Request count by status\n- `apiserver_client_certificate_expiration_seconds` - Client cert expiry\n- `etcd_db_total_size_in_bytes` - etcd storage size\n- `apiserver_cache_list_total_duration_seconds` - Cache performance\n\n**Health Checks:**\n- `/healthz` - Basic liveness (always up)\n- `/livez` - Liveness with startup grace period\n- `/readyz` - Readiness (post-start hooks done, storage ready)\n\n**Logging:**\n- Request path, method, status code logged at debug level\n- Errors logged with stack traces\n- Audit logging configured separately\n\n---\n\n## 7. Important Files and Directory Map\n\n### Core Server Components\n\n| File/Directory | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/server/config.go` | Config struct, DefaultBuildHandlerChain |\n| `pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` | GenericAPIServer, InstallAPIGroup(s) |\n| `pkg/server/plugins.go` | Built-in admission plugin registration |\n| `pkg/server/handler.go` | APIServerHandler, mux routing |\n| `pkg/server/routes/` | Health checks, profiling, discovery |\n| `pkg/server/options/` | Command-line flag parsing (RecommendedOptions) |\n\n### Handler Chain and Filters\n\n| File/Directory | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/endpoints/filters/` | Auth, authz, audit, deadline filters |\n| `pkg/server/filters/` | CORS, timeout, panic recovery, priority/fairness |\n| `pkg/endpoints/filterlatency/` | Latency tracking between filters |\n| `pkg/server/mux/` | HTTP mux and path registration |\n\n### REST Handlers\n\n| File/Directory | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/endpoints/installer.go` | APIInstaller, HTTP endpoint registration |\n| `pkg/endpoints/handlers/` | GET, LIST, POST, PATCH, DELETE, WATCH handlers |\n| `pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/` | Server-side apply field tracking |\n| `pkg/endpoints/request/` | RequestInfo, scope naming |\n\n### Storage\n\n| File/Directory | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/storage/interfaces.go` | Storage interface, versioning, selection predicates |\n| `pkg/storage/etcd3/` | etcd v3 backend implementation |\n| `pkg/storage/cacher/` | Watch cache implementation |\n| `pkg/storage/value/` | Encryption/transformation pipeline |\n| `pkg/registry/generic/` | Generic storage registry |\n| `pkg/registry/rest/` | REST storage interfaces |\n\n### Authentication & Authorization\n\n| File/Directory | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/authentication/authenticator/` | Authenticator interface |\n| `pkg/authentication/authenticatorfactory/` | Wiring authenticators (certs, tokens, OIDC) |\n| `pkg/authentication/request/` | Request authenticators (bearer, basic, header) |\n| `pkg/authorization/authorizer/` | Authorizer interface |\n| `pkg/authorization/` | RBAC, node, webhook authorizers |\n\n### Admission Control\n\n| File/Directory | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/admission/interfaces.go` | Admission plugin interface |\n| `pkg/admission/handler.go` | Admission handler base class |\n| `pkg/admission/chain.go` | Admission chain execution |\n| `pkg/admission/plugin/` | Built-in plugins (webhooks, lifecycle, policies) |\n| `pkg/admission/initializer/` | Plugin initialization with informers |\n\n### Audit & Logging\n\n| File/Directory | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/audit/` | Audit policy enforcement, event logging |\n| `pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go` | Audit filter hook |\n| `pkg/server/httplog/` | HTTP request logging |\n\n### Utilities\n\n| File/Directory | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/util/flowcontrol/` | Priority & fairness implementation |\n| `pkg/features/` | Feature gates (APIServerTracing, etc.) |\n| `pkg/storageversion/` | Storage version tracking |\n| `pkg/endpoints/openapi/` | OpenAPI spec generation |\n| `pkg/endpoints/discovery/` | Resource discovery (`/apis`) |\n\n### Documentation\n\n| File | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `ARCHITECTURE.md` | High-level architecture (server chain, handler flow) |\n| `README.md` | Purpose and usage notes |\n\n---\n\n## 8. Design Philosophy and Key Principles\n\n### 8.1 Generic and Pluggable\n\nThe apiserver is intentionally generic: it makes NO assumptions about resource types. All resources are treated uniformly:\n- Storage backends pluggable\n- Authentication/authorization policies pluggable\n- Admission webhooks pluggable\n- Handler chain customizable\n\nThis enables diversity: CRDs, extension apiservers, even non-Kubernetes APIs to use the same framework.\n\n### 8.2 HTTP/REST Semantics\n\nAll resources exposed as HTTP endpoints with REST semantics:\n- GET (retrieve), POST (create), PUT (replace), PATCH (update), DELETE\n- Standard HTTP status codes (200, 201, 404, 409, 429, 500)\n- Content negotiation (JSON, protobuf, YAML)\n- Watch via `?watch=true` \u2192 persistent connection with streaming JSON\n\nThis makes apiserver usable by any HTTP client without Kubernetes-specific libraries.\n\n### 8.3 Storage Abstraction\n\nStorage is an interface, not a concrete implementation:\n- etcd v3 is the production backend\n- Watch cache is an optional wrapper\n- Encryption is a storage transformer\n- Custom backends can be plugged in\n\nThis separation of concerns enables storage agility without changing API semantics.\n\n### 8.4 Concurrency and Fair Scheduling\n\nThe apiserver expects high concurrency. Multiple mechanisms ensure fairness:\n- Flow control: classify requests and queue by priority\n- Timeouts: long-running requests detected and isolated\n- Rate limiting: max concurrent requests per verb/resource\n- Watch cache: reduces load amplification\n\nThe goal: one user's workload should not starve others.\n\n### 8.5 Optimistic Concurrency\n\nNo pessimistic locking (row-level locks in DB). Instead:\n- Every object has immutable `resourceVersion` (etcd mod_revision)\n- Clients perform read-modify-write with version check\n- Server rejects if version mismatch \u2192 client retries\n\nThis maximizes concurrency and avoids deadlocks.\n\n### 8.6 Metadata-Driven Policy\n\nPolicies (RBAC, admission) expressed as Kubernetes resources, not config files:\n- Roles/RoleBindings define permissions\n- WebhookConfiguration resources define admission webhooks\n- APIServiceConfiguration resources define extension servers\n\nThis allows policies to be versioned, audited, and changed dynamically without restarting apiserver.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Common Integration Patterns\n\n### 9.1 Building a Custom API Server\n\n```go\n// Create config\nconfig := genericapiserver.NewConfig(serializer.CodecFactory{...})\nconfig.Authentication.Authenticator = myAuthenticator\nconfig.Authorization.Authorizer = myAuthorizer\nconfig.AdmissionControl = myAdmissionChain\n\n// Create server\nserver, err := config.Complete(nil).New(\"my-server\", genericapiserver.NewEmptyDelegate())\n\n// Register API groups\nserver.InstallAPIGroup(&myAPIGroupInfo)\n\n// Start server\nprepared := server.PrepareRun()\nprepared.Run(stopCh)\n```\n\n### 9.2 Custom Storage Backend\n\nImplement `storage.Interface` with your storage backend:\n```go\ntype MyStorage struct {\n    db MyDatabase\n}\n\nfunc (ms *MyStorage) Get(ctx context.Context, key string, opts storage.GetOptions, out runtime.Object) error {\n    // Query MyDatabase, populate out\n    return nil\n}\n\n// ... implement all Interface methods ...\n```\n\nThen pass to `genericregistry.Store`.\n\n### 9.3 Adding a Custom Admission Webhook\n\n```go\napiserver.AddPostStartHook(\"setup-webhooks\", func(ctx PostStartHookContext) error {\n    // Create ValidatingWebhookConfiguration resource\n    config := &admissionregistrationv1.ValidatingWebhookConfiguration{\n        ObjectMeta: metav1.ObjectMeta{Name: \"my-webhook\"},\n        Webhooks: []admissionregistrationv1.ValidatingWebhook{{\n            Name: \"my.example.com\",\n            ClientConfig: admissionregistrationv1.WebhookClientConfig{\n                URL: stringPtr(\"https://my-webhook-server/validate\"),\n            },\n            Rules: []admissionregistrationv1.RuleWithOperations{{\n                Operations: []admissionregistrationv1.OperationType{\"CREATE\", \"UPDATE\"},\n                Rule: admissionregistrationv1.Rule{\n                    APIGroups: []string{\"apps\"},\n                    Resources: []string{\"deployments\"},\n                },\n            }},\n            FailurePolicy: &failPolicy,\n        }},\n    }\n\n    client := ctx.LoopbackClientConfig.ClientForUser(...)\n    validatingWebhooks := client.AdmissionregistrationV1().ValidatingWebhookConfigurations()\n    _, err := validatingWebhooks.Create(context.TODO(), config, metav1.CreateOptions{})\n    return err\n})\n```\n\n### 9.4 Custom Request Filtering\n\nWrap the default handler chain:\n\n```go\nconfig.BuildHandlerChainFunc = func(apiHandler http.Handler, c *genericapiserver.Config) http.Handler {\n    handler := apiHandler\n\n    // Add custom filter\n    handler = http.HandlerFunc(func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {\n        // Custom logic\n        if shouldBlock(r) {\n            w.WriteHeader(http.StatusForbidden)\n            return\n        }\n        handler.ServeHTTP(w, r)\n    })\n\n    // Then apply defaults\n    handler = genericapiserver.DefaultBuildHandlerChain(handler, c)\n\n    return handler\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 10. Conclusion\n\nThe Kubernetes apiserver library provides a robust, extensible framework for building HTTP APIs with Kubernetes semantics. Its strength lies in the separation of concerns:\n- **Server infrastructure** (GenericAPIServer) handles lifecycle, discovery, registration\n- **Handler chain** manages authentication, authorization, admission as composable filters\n- **Storage abstraction** allows multiple backends without changing API semantics\n- **Plugin system** (admission webhooks, authorizers, authenticators) enables customization without code changes\n\nUnderstanding the request flow through the handler chain and the role of each component is key to customizing the apiserver safely. The extension points are deliberately chosen to balance flexibility with safety; most customization happens outside the core server code via webhooks and configuration.\n\nFor detailed implementation patterns, refer to the ARCHITECTURE.md file and the kube-apiserver source code in `cmd/kube-apiserver/app/`, which demonstrates how to compose the core apiserver with extensions (API Extensions for CRDs, kube-aggregator for third-party APIs) into a complete API server.\n",
